< text>
Holy Guacamole Batman! This place is amazing!

There is care and consideration from the atmosphere to the food we ordered to the price point.

If you haven't tried Craft Burrito you simply must.

If you have visitors coming from out of town, if you're hungry for a huge meal, if you're not that hungry but need to eat something and have extra for tomorrow... Any reason you have to eat out -- go here.

Update 3/19: The owner is friendly and personally made sure we were completely satisfied with our meal.

He brought out this incredible sauce from the kitchen. It has a slow burn but oh, so yummy. Highly recommended!< /text>

<userid>114243952563718809248<//userid>< username>
Jon Pratt< /username>
<Date>1560658444500< /Date><Rate>5< /Rate>< text>
Super solid Calexico comida.  Tacos, burritos and SoCal craft brew. The menu is streamlined but the result is a small selection of well made calexican dishes

I had the nacho fries which come with carnitas, chicken and carne asada (yes that's how they come).  My wife had a bowl - they have custom-order burrito bowls for those of you that are health conscious.

The feel is boutique-sports-bar with comfortable log-bench seating and plenty of televisores.  There's an outdoor courtyard area if you want to dine al fresco, however, there are no outdoor TVs if you're visiting for a game.

Wasn't  packed when we went so enjoy it while it lasts.</text>

< user>
112838591816302967370< /user>
<Name>Justin Jones< /Name><Date>1546471008396< /Date>< rating>
2</rating>
<Text>Craft Burrito is suffering from an identity crisis. Is it a craft beer bar that serves burritos and apps or a burrito spot that pours beers? When I read the signage "Craft Burrito Company" I thought the former. When I walked in for lunch today, I immediately thought the later. Emphasis matters because it totally tees up the customers expectations. Today, I am not sure Craft Burrito Company knows what it wants to be.

When I first walked in I thought, "the atmosphere is stellar!" Craft Burrito Co. showcases a great rustic/modern theme. A designer was likely consulted in the construction of the restaurant as the visual polish pulled off here is impressive, especially for a competitor of Chipotle. After such a fantastic first impression I began to think, "If the food gets the same attention to detail as the interior I am in for a real treat!"

For Temecula, It was a colder winter morning - 59F outside at lunch time. Strangely, my wife and I noticed the A/C was on. We opted to sit outside where it was more comfortable in the sun. My wife ordered the "Del Mar" and I ordered the Hot Buggy.

The food came in an acceptable amount of time, It arrived in square metal trays, burritos wrapped up in foil and served next to some chips. Nice touch keeping the trays warm. That may read strangely but it was cold in the restaurant and outside so I appreciated the warmth.

Unfortunately, the food did not deliver. The Del Mar consisted of (undercooked/hard) brown rice, 4 shrimps (really?), and a small handful of peppers and onions. It was such a strange experience. I took one bite and immediately had so many questions... First off, why is this a burrito and not a bowl? Secondly, why make it so large if 90% of it is just plain brown rice? and Third, what is this "craft sauce"?

The menu lays the foundation for a standard seafood burrito - "Grilled shrimp, rice, bell peppers, onions, and craft sauce." Craft sauce, what does that mean to you? My expectations were more aligned with a buttery, citrusy bright marinade to really let the shrimp pop. Instead I got a smoky, creamy, deep experience. A strange blend of BBQ sauce, Cream, and Chipotle Mayo maybe? Not horrible, but the wrong way to take a shrimp burrito in my opinion.

(the workers did check on us and replaced the burrito with a different option when they heard the rice was undercooked ++)

Next was the Hot Buggy. Someone on Facebook posted this burrito which is what inspired my journey to Craft Burrito in the first place. The Hot Buggy certainly was the better of the two choices but I wouldn't order it again. Pork, Potatoes, Red Chili (not green?) and Cheese. A potentially brilliant combination if executed well but it just was okay. The most notable thing for me was the potatoes. If I had to guess, they were browned with the chili sauce. It gave the potatoes a unique bright orange color and an nice crusty texture but they were very heavy. It reminded me of the way greasy spoons some times serve their chili. The bun takes on a neon orange color from the chili powder in the fat. Some people really like that style of cooking ala "The Hat", or "Tommys". I wasn't feeling it. Very one dimensional in flavor compared to the almost intimidating red and orange color.

If Craft Burritos dropped "Burritos" from their brand and menu their reviews may tell a different story - Craft, a quaint little beer bar with decent bites and a fun way to spend a Saturday afternoon. As long as the word "Burrito" exists in their name, and they are going after the coveted lunch hour business, Craft Burrito Company is setting themselves up for more bad reviews and disappointed customers.<//Text><Pictures>None<//Pictures>< Resp>
None< /Resp>

< Review>
A quiet beach away from rush and crowd opposite to electrical or power plant. Kind of vintage look below hill some industry, road and long beach strip. El Segundo beach is clean and not crowded, might be because of covid. Beach area is not commercialized and hence you enjoy more with natural beauty. Good place to spent time with family and kids. To play volleyball and other beach side games with kids and friends. Sufficient Parking space which are paid.</Review>

0x80c2b16e02e508a7:0xe9c19a0bfda11fbe</gmap_id>
<Review>On a sunny and clear day, very few places are as beautiful as this long stretch of beach.
There's a bike/ running path along from El  Segundo down to Torrance beach.
Along the way, there's beautiful stretches of beach, some areas with huge waves (along El Porto).
The sandy area is wide, and in some parts, is quite a walk until you get to the shore.
The closer you are to LAX,  the more plane traffic you get to see which for me, is always a treat since I'm something of a plane spotter.
The water is cold most times, but you get acclimated to it. The waves and surf can be rough, so good swimming skills are a MUST in this stretch of beach/ocean.
You can find yourself very far from your beach spot if you don't mind your surroundings. Also, if you relax to much, you may find yourself well outside the point where the waves form and break, and swimming back may induce panic if you're not a seasoned swimmer so be careful.
Otherwise, this beach is awesome in every way from just going along for a walk, or spending a day in the water. People are everywhere, and there never a dull moment.
You can either pay and park in certain areas, or like me, just go during the week says when it is not packed and park along the residential areas, but PLEASE DO BE RESPECTFUL of the residents and their properties. Park mindfully, and be respectful.
And your day will be great!</Review><response>None</response>< Date>
1531264373018</Date>
